    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

<span id="freeTextContainer47473277888186045">At first, only a few things are known about the celestial object that astronomers dub Rama. It is huge, weighing more than ten trillion tons. And it is hurtling through the solar system at an inconceivable speed. Then a space probe confirms the unthinkable: Rama is no natural object. It is, incredibly, an interstellar spacecraft. Space explorers and planet-bound scientists</span>
  <span id="freeText47473277888186045" style="display:none">At first, only a few things are known about the celestial object that astronomers dub Rama. It is huge, weighing more than ten trillion tons. And it is hurtling through the solar system at an inconceivable speed. Then a space probe confirms the unthinkable: Rama is no natural object. It is, incredibly, an interstellar spacecraft. Space explorers and planet-bound scientists alike prepare for mankind's first encounter with alien intelligence. It will kindle their wildest dreams... and fan their darkest fears. For no one knows who the Ramans are or why they have come. And now the moment of rendezvous awaits — just behind a Raman airlock door.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/847726-is-the-science-in-this-book-dated-the">Is the &quot;science&quot; in this book dated? The author wasn&#39;t even exposed to the basic technology we take for granted today such as smartphones, electric cars, etc. I&#39;d imagine that if someone picked up a book like The Martian 40 years from now they&#39;d find the science somewhat antiquated.</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/2457511-stebbins"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1556276374i/2457511._UY100_CR21,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/2457511-stebbins">Stebbins</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You're confusing science for technology. It seems obvious that the scientific principles underlying the technology are the same today as they were the<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You're confusing science for technology. It seems obvious that the scientific principles underlying the technology are the same today as they were then, even if technology you speak of itself didn't exist at the time of the book's writing.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div class='questionText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/1466920-i-must-have-missed-it-but-i-could-not"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I must have missed it but I could not understand why the folks on Mercury cared if Rama entered orbit around the sun. Why did they have such a hard deadline to do something by the time it reached perihelion? So what it it joined the orbit? Why could they not just nuke it then if it turned out to be hostile? I could not understand (or missed) the reasoning for this deadline. Can someone people help. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/85825923-ivanopinion"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/85825923-ivanopinion">IvanOpinion</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think it was that such an orbit would be within Hermian "jurisdiction", so they felt more able to assert their view that malign intentions should be<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think it was that such an orbit would be within Hermian "jurisdiction", so they felt more able to assert their view that malign intentions should be assumed. <br /><br />(Given the level of Raman technology, I'm pretty sure that Rama would have had self-defence capabilities easily able to foil a nuclear missile. I rather expected the plot would develop with the missile being detonated and having no effect or Rama's defences splatting the missile seconds before detonation.)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1498136569" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498136569" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1498136569?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1498136569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10407157000165303489">It's odd to think that this book was published 40 years ago. I don't know why that strikes me as strange, but it does.... <br/><br/>It's tempting for me to call this book "Traditional Science Fiction." Or "Classic Science Fiction" or something along those lines. But what I really mean to say is that this is a story where the science is one of the central aspects of the story. <br/><br/>The basic premise of the story is: In the future, humanity finds a alien spacecraft and investigates it. <br/><br/>A lot of the joy of explor</span>
  <span id="freeText10407157000165303489" style="display:none">It's odd to think that this book was published 40 years ago. I don't know why that strikes me as strange, but it does.... <br /><br />It's tempting for me to call this book "Traditional Science Fiction." Or "Classic Science Fiction" or something along those lines. But what I really mean to say is that this is a story where the science is one of the central aspects of the story. <br /><br />The basic premise of the story is: In the future, humanity finds a alien spacecraft and investigates it. <br /><br />A lot of the joy of exploration comes from the theory of how a spaceship might really work in terms of physics. How could you generate gravity on a spaceship? How would it travel? What would the aliens be like? What would the purpose of these various pieces of the ships be? (Such as, for example, a large body of water, or featureless buildings on an island?<br /><br />It's an interesting story, but probably *mostly* interesting for people interested in the genuine science of interstellar/interplanetary travel.<br /><br />For example, if you enjoyed The Martian, you have a good chance of liking this book. (But be warned, the pacing is much different than The Martian. It's not First Person. It's not conversational. It's not painfully technical, but it was written in a different age.<br /><br />Of particular interest to me was the fact that many of the smaller plot arcs of the books were very short. By which I mean to say that when a problem arises in the story, the resolution comes very soon afterwards. That limits the tension of the story somewhat, as you don't have time to get too worried over anything before it's fixed. <br /><br />Lastly, it's important to note that this book ends with many questions unanswered. But the good news is that there are two more books in the series that will explore those questions further, and I trust Clarke to pay me off with good answers by the end of the series.<br /><br />***<br /><br />Later edit: I read the sequel, and I have to retract my previous statement. The follow-up book severely damaged my opinion of this book to the point where I don't know if I would reccomend it any more.<br /><br />So if you were considering reading this book based on my review, you might want to read this first in order to get the whole story... <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1518547029">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10407157000165303489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192068378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer471118375933865513">Mysterious and engaging, classic science fiction.<br/><br/>I first read this back in high school, we'll just say a LONG time ago. Since then the concepts, ideas and themes surrounding this archetypal work of science fiction have been a huge influence on works in this genre. Clarke first published this Hugo and Nebula award winner in 1972. The first works that I think of that was influenced by RWR is John Varley's excellent <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49838.Titan__Gaea___1_' title='Titan (Gaea, #1) by John Varley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Titan</a> series, first coming out in 1979. His influence on Ridley Scott's Alien, also</span>
  <span id="freeText471118375933865513" style="display:none">Mysterious and engaging, classic science fiction.<br><br>I first read this back in high school, we'll just say a LONG time ago. Since then the concepts, ideas and themes surrounding this archetypal work of science fiction have been a huge influence on works in this genre. Clarke first published this Hugo and Nebula award winner in 1972. The first works that I think of that was influenced by RWR is John Varley's excellent <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49838.Titan__Gaea___1_" title="Titan (Gaea, #1) by John Varley" rel="nofollow noopener">Titan</a> series, first coming out in 1979. His influence on Ridley Scott's Alien, also released in 1979, is clear. <br><br>What Clarke did was to affirm that there are and remain mysteries that we will not get, that there are some aspects of scientific research and observation that will remain over our heads.<br><br>******2017 reread – I’m advancing my rating, giving this a 5 star. I recall liking it as a younger man, but this is premier, elite SF. <br><br>Clarke deservedly won the SF triple crown for this work – Hugo, Nebula and John W. Campbell – as well as a host of other awards including the Locus and British SF Association Award. It’s that good. It should be on a short list of best SF ever.<br><br>Clarke’s Rama has all of what’s best in a SF story: future science, intrepid explorers, contact with aliens, space, rockets, and mystery. That last element is what wins here, we know about the Ramans, but not all about them by a long shot, there is still much more to know. He has, and we have vicariously through his story, only just scratched the surface of knowledge and what is learned, decades worth of knowledge according to Commander Norman, only leads to more questions.<br><br>Excellent, Science Fiction of the highest order.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509576641i/24338398._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="295" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7432836643677904871">Rendezvous with Rama, Arthur C. Clarke<br/><br/>Rendezvous with Rama is a science fiction novel by British writer Arthur C. Clarke first published in 1973. Set in the 2130's, the story involves a 50-kilometre (31 mile) cylindrical alien starship that enters the Solar System. The story is told from the point of view of a group of human explorers who intercept the ship in an attempt to unlock its mysteries. The novel won both the Hugo and Nebula awards upon its release, and is regarded as one of the corners</span>
  <span id="freeText7432836643677904871" style="display:none">Rendezvous with Rama, Arthur C. Clarke<br /><br />Rendezvous with Rama is a science fiction novel by British writer Arthur C. Clarke first published in 1973. Set in the 2130's, the story involves a 50-kilometre (31 mile) cylindrical alien starship that enters the Solar System. The story is told from the point of view of a group of human explorers who intercept the ship in an attempt to unlock its mysteries. The novel won both the Hugo and Nebula awards upon its release, and is regarded as one of the cornerstones in Clarke's bibliography. The concept was later extended with several sequels.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: در سال 1995 میلادی<br /><br />این کتاب نخستین بار با ترجمه محمد قصاع در سال 1371 هجری خورشیدی در نشر افق نیز منتشر شده است<br /><br />عنوان: میعاد با راما ؛ نویسنده: آرتور سی. کلارک؛ مترجم: هرمز حبیبی اصفهانی؛ تهران نشر نقطه، 1374، در 268 ص، شابک: ایکس - 964554825<br /><br />ادامه این داستان با عنوان «راما 2» یا «ادامه میعاد با راما» با ترجمه ناصر بلیغ در نشر نقطه در سال 1375 در 494 ص به چاپ رسیده و به زیور طبع آراسته شده است شابک: 9645548276؛<br /><br />کتابهای «میعاد با راما»، «راما 2»، «باغ راما» و «راز راما»، سری چهار جلدی از آثار «آرتور سی. کلارک» هستند، مجموعه‌ ای بیهمتا که به روشنی، نمایانگر چیره‌ دستی «کلارک»، در آفرینش داستان‌های علمی-تخیلی هستند. «میعاد با راما»، در 350 صفحه است و آغاز این ماجراست. …؛ «راما» سفینه‌ ای غول پیکر، و استوانه‌ ای شکل است، که با سرعت سرسام آوری، گرد محور خویش می‌چرخد. …؛ از بیکران‌ها، گام در منظومه ی شمسی می‌نهد، و دانشمندان آن روزگاران را، انگشت به دهان می‌سازد. ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_68550667" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Cassy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2282938-cassy"><img alt="Cassy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565892954p2/2282938.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553287899" href="/book/show/774928.Rendezvous_with_Rama">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=physical-own">physical-own</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68550667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8032517094594463283">Ladies, have you ever heard the advice that the more you cover up, the sexier you are? Forgo the plunging neckline for the small keyhole. Let the boys use their imagination. Hint, but don’t show. <br/><br/>Clarke evidently had. He dressed this book in a turtleneck, elbow-length gloves, trousers, work boots, and one of those hats with ear flaps. There is barely any flesh showing. What does show <i>is</i> intriguing – a mysterious spaceship, a beautiful flower, an unknown destination, buildings with no doors or wi</span>
  <span id="freeText8032517094594463283" style="display:none">Ladies, have you ever heard the advice that the more you cover up, the sexier you are? Forgo the plunging neckline for the small keyhole. Let the boys use their imagination. Hint, but don’t show. <br /><br />Clarke evidently had. He dressed this book in a turtleneck, elbow-length gloves, trousers, work boots, and one of those hats with ear flaps. There is barely any flesh showing. What does show <i>is</i> intriguing – a mysterious spaceship, a beautiful flower, an unknown destination, buildings with no doors or windows, living machines. But the book stops the courtship at the flirting stage. Nothing happens. No answers. No aliens massacring the human exploration team. <br /><br />While this was a nice departure from books nowadays that reveal everything, it was ultimately unsatisfying. Clarke withheld too much for me to really enjoy the book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8032517094594463283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_159504936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159504936" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159504936?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345315601" href="/book/show/917367.Rendezvous_with_Rama">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=list-of-shame">list-of-shame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=oldies">oldies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159504936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer302879779890530538">An enormous alien structure enters our solar system and a team is dispatched to explore it before it drifts away and is lost forever. What will humanity discover after its Rendezvous with Rama?<br/><br/>Years ago, I decided I needed to read more hard science fiction. Then I read Ringworld and was so uninterested that I quit my hard sf quest before it began. Months ago, a copy of Rendezvous with Rama fell into my clutches. I decided to give it a try, despite my fears that it would be another Ringworld, a b</span>
  <span id="freeText302879779890530538" style="display:none">An enormous alien structure enters our solar system and a team is dispatched to explore it before it drifts away and is lost forever. What will humanity discover after its Rendezvous with Rama?<br /><br />Years ago, I decided I needed to read more hard science fiction. Then I read Ringworld and was so uninterested that I quit my hard sf quest before it began. Months ago, a copy of Rendezvous with Rama fell into my clutches. I decided to give it a try, despite my fears that it would be another Ringworld, a book where the concept far outweighs the story. Well, the concepts behind Rendezvous with Rama do outweigh the story but I found it far superior to Ringworld, a much more enjoyable reading experience. <br /><br />As near as I can tell, Rendezvous with Rama is the first Big Dumb Object (or Megastructure, if you prefer) science fiction novel. For that reason alone, I'd say it's worth a read. Hell, that's why I read it.<br /><br />The characters are weak but I think that's actually an asset for a story like this. My problem with Ringworld was that I didn't find any of the characters likeable and that overshadowed any sense of discovery I would have felt as they explored Ringworld. In Rama, the characters take a back seat to the Big Dumb Object from the first page. <br /><br />Clarke's writing is workmanlike but does a surprisingly good job at conveying the wonder and majesty of Rama as the team explores it. As things heat up the closer Rama gets to the sun (see what I did there?), the book really takes off.<br /><br />With today's special effects technology, I think it would be fantastic if an adaptation was filmed like a faux-documentary. Like that Mermaid one National Geographic put out, only not so cheesey.<br /><br />I liked it but I didn't love it. There's not a lot of plot or character development. Or action, for that matter. Now that I've read it, I respect its place in the hard science fiction pantheon but the sense of wonder doesn't make up for its shortcomings so a three is as high as I can give it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="302879779890530538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_421123200" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421123200" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421123200?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421123200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5952106604269939064">We, the humanity, see quite a lot of comets and meteors flying around. So in the future (fairly distant) nobody cared much about yet another such visitor until astronomers realized it had an ideal cylindrical form. At this point it did not take a genius to realize its artificial origin. Luckily there was a spaceship nearby to catch up with the guest (named Rama) <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520044456i/25152606._SX540_.jpg' alt='Rama' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>before it disappears into depths of space. This is the story about the ship's crew exploring dead alien derelict and the reaction of th</span>
  <span id="freeText5952106604269939064" style="display:none">We, the humanity, see quite a lot of comets and meteors flying around. So in the future (fairly distant) nobody cared much about yet another such visitor until astronomers realized it had an ideal cylindrical form. At this point it did not take a genius to realize its artificial origin. Luckily there was a spaceship nearby to catch up with the guest (named Rama) <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520044456i/25152606._SX540_.jpg" alt="Rama" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>before it disappears into depths of space. This is the story about the ship's crew exploring dead alien derelict and the reaction of the rest of the humans to their findings. <br><br>The real rating is not 5 stars by the way; it is only 4.5. The characters were quite flat and not exactly life-like. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520044663i/25152619._SX540_.jpg" alt="Flat characters" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>For this reason I understand why some readers did not like the book. It is however not about people. It is about incomprehensible wonders of alien technology - just hasty brief glimpses of it.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520044781i/25152621._SX540_.jpg" alt="Alien technology" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This sense of wonder present through the whole book and that is the reason for the high rating. I can only recall one other science fiction book which has the same sense of alien wonders: Roadside Picnic (Red's Zone adventures to be exact). <br><br>Arthur C. Clark does outstanding job between being descriptive, but not overly so. His descriptions are brief enough to never become boring, yet they always give you good picture of what the explorers see. This takes some real skill to accomplish. Modern popular writers fall into two extremes when it comes to descriptions: non-stop absolutely unnecessary long ones (George R.R. Martin), or no descriptions whatsoever (Steven Erikson). My advice to both of these guys: read this book and learn. Read it one more time and learn better. Continue reading it until you are able to deliver an excellent tale in under 150 pages. <br><br>So if you are looking for great flawed characters look elsewhere. Otherwise the story is really good and highly recommended. The common wisdom is that the following books are much weaker. Unlike this one they are written in collaboration with Gentry Lee and collaborations rarely work, in my opinion. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520045026i/25152660._SX540_.jpg" alt="Collaboration" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Reading the descriptions of the book 2 and its reviews I became convinced that I am not interested to continue the series. Fortunately first book works well as a standalone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5952106604269939064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2472193513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2472193513" />
    <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton"><img alt="J.L.   Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438142892p2/3675162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2472193513?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.L.   Sutton" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton">J.L.   Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2472193513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11512478203957431923">There was just enough detail to go with the all the mystery behind the alien ship hurtling through the solar system to make Arthur C. Clarke’s Rendezvous with Rama an engaging and thought provoking read! Other than a spaceflight to intercept and explore the huge Raman spacecraft, there’s very little action in this novel and (unfortunately) very little character development. I do think there is a sense of wonder about the possibilities contained in the mysterious ship. The book whets your appetit</span>
  <span id="freeText11512478203957431923" style="display:none">There was just enough detail to go with the all the mystery behind the alien ship hurtling through the solar system to make Arthur C. Clarke’s Rendezvous with Rama an engaging and thought provoking read! Other than a spaceflight to intercept and explore the huge Raman spacecraft, there’s very little action in this novel and (unfortunately) very little character development. I do think there is a sense of wonder about the possibilities contained in the mysterious ship. The book whets your appetite to get to the bottom of some of the mysteries contained on the Raman spacecraft and maybe even meet some actual Ramans, but (given that the ship has a limited amount of time in the solar system), there are lots of unanswered questions. While Clarke doesn’t explain all the mysteries, that’s also a strength of the novel. We as readers supply some of our own answers about the possibilities. This makes Rendezvous with Rama an engaging read! <br /><br />3.75 stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11512478203957431923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_206734338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206734338" />
    <a title="Apatt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt"><img alt="Apatt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349239948p2/2457095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206734338?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Apatt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Apatt" href="/user/show/2457095-apatt">Apatt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206734338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17107658240248395256">Rendezvous With Rama starts off where lesser books would climax. To begin with parts of Italy are wiped out by an asteroid leading to the creation of the Spaceguard system for detecting future asteroids well in advance of collision so that preventative measures can be taken. Along comes another huge object initially mistaken for another asteroid but as it draws nearer turns out to be a ginormous spaceship with no apparent mean of propulsion. The ship is given the named Rama and the crew of Earth</span>
  <span id="freeText17107658240248395256" style="display:none">Rendezvous With Rama starts off where lesser books would climax. To begin with parts of Italy are wiped out by an asteroid leading to the creation of the Spaceguard system for detecting future asteroids well in advance of collision so that preventative measures can be taken. Along comes another huge object initially mistaken for another asteroid but as it draws nearer turns out to be a ginormous spaceship with no apparent mean of propulsion. The ship is given the named Rama and the crew of Earth's survey ship Endeavour land on it and enter to investigate.<br><br>This is the father of the popular <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_Dumb_Object" rel="nofollow noopener">Big Dumb Object</a> sci-fi trope which features humongous alien artifacts befuddling humanity when they are discovered or unexpectedly show up. I just reread this book immediately after finishing another BDO classic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/401161761" rel="nofollow noopener">Gateway by Frederik Pohl</a>. Gateway totally confounded my expectation because while it features a BDO the focus of the book is on the impact of this object on the life of the protagonist. Being confounded in this case is not too unpleasant as Gateway is a good though provoking read. However, it still left me with a hankering for some BDO adventure and <i>Rendezvous With Rama</i> provided this in spades. This book really is what it says on the tin and if you are in the market for some jaw dropping sense of wonder this is the one to pick up.<br><br>Arthur C. Clarke was a stupendous writer of sf, unlike a lot of scientist sf authors he could write with excellent transparency and clarity of vision. He is particularly brilliant at describing the minutiae of space voyages; just the simple act of walking up and down stairs in near zero gravity can become a vivid and fascinating adventure in his stories. Certainly with "Rama" Clarke gets a lot of millage from the cylindrical shape of Rama, the gravitational and centrifugal effects, the weather, the visual impact of the north and south poles, the sea as a cylindrical band etc. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473215143i/20428036._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>My favourite Rama art by Jim Burns<br><br>That said it is worth noting that this is a novel of exploration, not essentially a pulse pounding action adventure on a dangerous planet, although there is an element of that also. The emphasis is more on the sense of wonder than sense of danger. There are many vividly imagined scenes in this book so clearly described that if you do an image search for "Rendezvous With Rama" on on Google you will find quite a few excellent artworks inspired by this book, a similar search on Youtube will also yield quite a few fan made videos (this <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZY2Yt1ATm4c" rel="nofollow noopener">short student film</a> is my favrorite).<br><br>As usual Clarke did not write with literary flourishes and characterization was clearly not a priority for him. I find the central characters of this book almost interchangeable in their blandness. However I am not sure this is a weakness of Clarke's writing because his books are generally not very long and by not allocating many pages on developing the characters he is able to do a lot of world building, describing the minutiae and implications of his settings, and a spring a few surprises on his readers from his plotting. <br><br>I feel that <i>Rendezvous With Rama</i> complements Phol's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/218427.Gateway__Heechee_Saga___1_" title="Gateway (Heechee Saga, #1) by Frederik Pohl" rel="nofollow noopener">Gateway</a> very nicely, one is about the BDO, the other is about the psychological impact of a BDO. I recommend reading both.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473215354i/20428047._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Another view of Rama (don't know who it's by, sorry).</span>
  <a data-text-id="17107658240248395256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Manuel Antão" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28709846-manuel-ant-o"><img alt="Manuel Antão" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504271107p2/28709846.jpg" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1239176209?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manuel Antão" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manuel Antão" href="/user/show/28709846-manuel-ant-o">Manuel Antão</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28709846-manuel-ant-o?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28709846-manuel-ant-o?shelf=2008">2008</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1239176209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1636265481989339410">If you're into stuff like this, <a href='https://manuelaantao.blogspot.pt/2018/03/workmanlike-prose-rendezvous-with-rama.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>you can read the full review.</a><br/><br/>Workmanlike Prose: "Rendezvous with Rama" by Arthur C. Clarke<br/><br/><br/>Ah, yes. Rama. I actually read this with a torch under the blankets in an intense all-nighter back in the day. What I like about this book in retrospect is its complete lack of compromise as a work of SF. Characters? Who the frack needs 'em. Themes? Bah, pointless! All SF needs to be is an unbroken, brilliantly done description of an alien environment. I'm glad things have mo</span>
  <span id="freeText1636265481989339410" style="display:none">If you're into stuff like this, <a href="https://manuelaantao.blogspot.pt/2018/03/workmanlike-prose-rendezvous-with-rama.html" rel="nofollow noopener">you can read the full review.</a><br /><br />Workmanlike Prose: "Rendezvous with Rama" by Arthur C. Clarke<br /><br /><br />Ah, yes. Rama. I actually read this with a torch under the blankets in an intense all-nighter back in the day. What I like about this book in retrospect is its complete lack of compromise as a work of SF. Characters? Who the frack needs 'em. Themes? Bah, pointless! All SF needs to be is an unbroken, brilliantly done description of an alien environment. I'm glad things have moved on since, but I'd still happily sit and read a book so single-mindedly in its purpose like this one.<br /> <br />In any genre of literature, you definitely have some people whose names tower above everyone else, and their influence could not be denied. However, people who like literature don't just read the so-called greats. Clarke certainly wrote some seminal works of SF, but he probably read many obscure works too, some of which may have influenced him. Readers don't just read the big name writers, but have a much bigger interest in the genre. A writer’s work only makes sense within a tradition and how it is situated along other people's work. It is all interlinked and some of the smaller voices may be bigger than critics acknowledge. For instance Clarke's influences aren't as well-known but what he learned from them is part of his work, so the voices remain powerful, and readers equally value preceding works. That doesn't mean that the big name writers don't deserve their place in history, but as fan of literature, I think sometimes, the bigger contributions are made by lesser known writers. I disagree with the assessment that Clarke left questions unanswered; world-building can get boring at the micro, non-plot-related level. This book was "sensawunda" in triplicate -- for the Ramans always did everything in threes. How about those tripodal cleansing things that whirled about? I'm not disappointed that Clarke had no sequel; when you look at 2001 on the screen, then read Clarke's rejected worlds, you realise that Kubrick was right to end with the “Star Child”. <br /> <br /> <br />If you're into SF, read on.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1636265481989339410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16271766093619486814">This book was <b>SO BORING.</b> Wow. <br/><br/>I did not care about any of these characters, they were only <i>slightly different</i> demeanor-wise, which I guess could be believable among astronauts, but it made for a really <b>lacking characterization</b> element.<br/><br/>Even during parts of the plot where danger was ensuing I felt no sense of danger & I had no feelings of hoping that the character in danger survived. <br/><br/>In this novel women hardly served a further purpose than to be a distraction for or sleep with the men. Sure they c</span>
  <span id="freeText16271766093619486814" style="display:none">This book was <b>SO BORING.</b> Wow. <br /><br />I did not care about any of these characters, they were only <i>slightly different</i> demeanor-wise, which I guess could be believable among astronauts, but it made for a really <b>lacking characterization</b> element.<br /><br />Even during parts of the plot where danger was ensuing I felt no sense of danger &amp; I had no feelings of hoping that the character in danger survived. <br /><br />In this novel women hardly served a further purpose than to be a distraction for or sleep with the men. Sure they carried titles of importance but their actions didn't line up with their titles. And the men they're distracting are some of the <b>flattest men I've ever read about</b> so it's kind of a stretch for me to believe anyone would want to sleep with them.<br /><br />The plot was also pretty <b>weak,</b> I never felt much of an urge to continue finding out what was going to happen. And then the end of book was entirely <b>anticlimactic.</b><br /><br />I know this is a huge classic amongst Sci-Fi lovers but I cannot even begin to understand which part everyone loves so much. On top of that, there is absolutely <b>zero payoff</b> for all that boring ass build up.<br /><br />I struggled through this book at the recommendation of a friend. I've read that the next books are much better &amp; that Clarke had a co-writer with him. I may give the sequel a chance but only after I've gargled a gallon of Listerine to get the bad taste out of my mouth. </span>

<div id="review_1597633534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1597633534" />
    <a title="Gary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30706026-gary"><img alt="Gary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465615148p2/30706026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1597633534?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary" href="/user/show/30706026-gary">Gary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1597633534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6953565307215212074">I originally read this in junior high, when I first eagerly devoured all the writings of the "Big 3". This reread is part of a project to revisit the classics I read in my youth, now with my pesky adult brain in tow.<br/>Rendezvous with Rama is pretty much the prototype for what people complain about when they say "they don't make 'em like they used to." It is also, by consequence, exactly what others are criticizing when they say "they shouldn't make 'em like that anymore." It is essentially a hard </span>
  <span id="freeText6953565307215212074" style="display:none">I originally read this in junior high, when I first eagerly devoured all the writings of the "Big 3". This reread is part of a project to revisit the classics I read in my youth, now with my pesky adult brain in tow.<br />Rendezvous with Rama is pretty much the prototype for what people complain about when they say "they don't make 'em like they used to." It is also, by consequence, exactly what others are criticizing when they say "they shouldn't make 'em like that anymore." It is essentially a hard sci-fi narrative centered around scientific discovery and methodical problem solving by its hyper-competent hero(es). It is an exciting story filled with all manner of wondrous events and inventions and landscapes to explore, and can easily be enjoyed at face value, hence the four stars. It's a darn good read, no question.<br />What I have recently noticed upon re-evaluating our holy trinity of Clarke, Asimov, and Heinlein, is that their sins were the collective sins of the Anglo-American golden age of sci-fi. There is very little in the way of emotional engagement with the characters, and Clarke in particular seems to regard other humans and their behavior with clinical interest at most - as if the inner life of his characters is only a necessary component of their existence insofar as it can explain their choices or their responses to stimuli. The social sciences were also poorly represented by these authors and their colleagues; being almost wholly obsessed with hard science, their future histories feel more like they were engineered in a controlled experiment, rather than having developed from any of the cultural conflicts and movements that really shape history. Science fiction will always date badly in some ways, because speculating about the future based on present day understandings is never going to be 100% accurate; however, the future society posited in Rendezvous with Rama is impossibly naïve in its conception and comes across as surprisingly reactionary, especially since Clarke was usually lumped in with the political left in the SF community.<br />I know, I know, "That's just how things were done back then!" There were plenty of writers from the olden timey days who didn't, though. There's a reason why John W. Campbell hated PKD's writing, for example. And also, there are plenty of authors who still do it that way (have you read Neal Stephenson?)<br />As a time capsule work, though, Rama is almost peerless in its execution, and definitely worth the read, even if our modernized adult brains have to let a few things slide to make it work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6953565307215212074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_41622979" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41622979" />
    <a title="Scurra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1350905-scurra"><img alt="Scurra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470522840p2/1350905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41622979?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scurra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scurra" href="/user/show/1350905-scurra">Scurra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1350905-scurra?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41622979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3083701744794093010">For heaven's sake, don't expect great writing from this book. For all his talent, Clarke wasn't a wordsmith (heck, even Asimov could write better!) <br/>Instead, simply glory in one of the cleverest conceits you will ever read - an encounter with an alien civilisation in which the aliens are absent and there is no convenient "universal translator" to explain things. Slowly you can begin to piece things together, keeping maybe one step ahead of the astronauts, but you become aware that trying to under</span>
  <span id="freeText3083701744794093010" style="display:none">For heaven's sake, don't expect great writing from this book. For all his talent, Clarke wasn't a wordsmith (heck, even Asimov could write better!) <br />Instead, simply glory in one of the cleverest conceits you will ever read - an encounter with an alien civilisation in which the aliens are absent and there is no convenient "universal translator" to explain things. Slowly you can begin to piece things together, keeping maybe one step ahead of the astronauts, but you become aware that trying to understand Raman culture is like trying to appreciate the Sistene Chapel ceiling without ever having read the Bible - you could create an explanation, but it would be utterly and magnificently wrong.<br /><br />All I ask is that you don't make the mistake of going on and reading the pointless sequels. Yes, I understand why they were written, but I can never forgive them for ruining the magic of the original. Just take this one and enjoy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3083701744794093010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3362260075" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3362260075" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3536004-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535136437p2/3536004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3362260075?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/3536004-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575077331" href="/book/show/112538.Rendezvous_with_Rama">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3536004-jenna?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3536004-jenna?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3362260075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15246667689748324321"><b>"The long-hoped-for, long-feared encounter had come at last. Mankind was about to receive the first visitor from the stars."</b><br/><br/>Watching the launch of SpaceX Falcon 9 yesterday, I was thrilled and mesmerized and briefly able to forget all the other shit that's happening in the world. <br/><br/>When I came back down to earth, I just couldn't stop wondering what we humans could do if we put aside our hatred and intolerance and began working together as one human race.<br/><br/>Here we are sending two astronauts back into</span>
  <span id="freeText15246667689748324321" style="display:none"><b>"The long-hoped-for, long-feared encounter had come at last. Mankind was about to receive the first visitor from the stars."</b><br><br>Watching the launch of SpaceX Falcon 9 yesterday, I was thrilled and mesmerized and briefly able to forget all the other shit that's happening in the world. <br><br>When I came back down to earth, I just couldn't stop wondering what we humans could do if we put aside our hatred and intolerance and began working together as one human race.<br><br>Here we are sending two astronauts back into space, to a life-sustaining station we have built up there. We have put men (next we need a woman!) on the moon and created robots that we sent to explore Mars. <br><br>So much we have done. And yet....... <br><br>After watching the launch, I had a quick foray through my Facebook feed only to be overcome with sadness and anger at all the injustice in this world. All the racism, the hatred, the murder. Instead of working for the better of the human race, instead of fighting our common enemy Covid19, we have here in the US another cop killing a Black man for the crime of too much melanin. Another. <br><br>When will it end?<br><br>It didn't end with the abolishment of slavery. It didn't end with the Civil Rights movement. It didn't end when America elected our first Black president. <br><br><b>It didn't end.</b><br><br>And so it was with relief that I picked up my Kindle and escaped back into the future. A future where humans have colonized our solar system and have hopefully begun seeing and treating each other as equals. <br><br>I enjoyed <i>Rendezvous with Rama</i>. It is at times slow-moving and yet this is necessary to set the scene for the following three books in the series. <br><br>It was exciting to go along as astronauts explored this unknown space-world, discovering what they could about the species who built it. It is likely millions of years old and no life remains; the ship is sterile. <br><br>Our main character draws parallels to the voyages of James Cook, as he and his team begin traversing this cylindrical world. I enjoyed following this expedition much more than I do sci-fi in which humans and alien life forms are in a galactic battle, using lasers and other advanced technology to kill each other. <br><br>It's not all a bed of roses though, and there are unforeseen dangers awaiting them as they try to learn what they can and solve the mystery of who built this space-faring world.<br><br>Unfortunately, the underlying sexism that permeates much of classic science fiction poked its ugly head into this story. I guess we haven't reached true equality for everyone after all. <br><br>Commander Norton, who is leading this excursion into Rama, feels that attractive, shapely women, "should not be allowed aboard ship; weightlessness did things to their breasts that were too damn distracting".<br><br>Eye roll, WTF, SMH, Sigh....... 🙄<br><br>Oddly(?), these humans of the future also felt the need to force others into a life of subjection and slavery. This made absolutely no sense to me. They have advanced technology that allows them to traverse and colonize the solar system and yet, instead of artificially intelligent robots to do the menial work aboard the ship, they genetically modify chimps to raise their IQs, enabling them to do all the cooking and cleaning and dirty work. These superchimps are obviously not free and though we see no violence enacted against them, it is still a form of slavery of another intelligent and sentient being. <br><br>Arther C. Clarke couldn't possibly have envisioned intelligent non-sentient robots in their stead?? Isn't he the one who created Hal 9000?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1590931226ra/29571275.gif" width="235" height="235" alt="Im Sorry Dave Im Afraid ICant Do That GIF - ImSorryDave ImAfraidICantDoThat GIFs" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Shame, shame, shame. I would have been OK with this in the story if even just one person spoke out against it and Clarke used it to point out the evils of slavery. Instead, it seemed normal and acceptable to all.<br><br>While I enjoyed exploring the alien world of the Ramans and wonder from where it came, I'm not sure I will continue the series.  I like science fiction that is more political (and more scientific).... showing the ills of our current society and how they might be amended.  I want to be able to escape the evils of our present world when I read science fiction, not read more of it.<br><br>3.5 stars rounded up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15246667689748324321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229314303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229314303" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229314303?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=scifi-60s-70s-80s">scifi-60s-70s-80s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229314303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6179858910794906206">i like world-building in science fiction and fantasy. in these modern times, extensive world-building is commonly derided... it is often seen as a lazy way to create a world, telling not showing, an author so in love with something they've built that they just want to describe instead of allowing the reader to slowly experience. i understand that point of view; world-building can often be seen as a glorified, masturbatory info-dump. but for some reason, it just doesn't bother me too much. i thin</span>
  <span id="freeText6179858910794906206" style="display:none">i like world-building in science fiction and fantasy. in these modern times, extensive world-building is commonly derided... it is often seen as a lazy way to create a world, telling not showing, an author so in love with something they've built that they just want to describe instead of allowing the reader to slowly experience. i understand that point of view; world-building can often be seen as a glorified, masturbatory info-dump. but for some reason, it just doesn't bother me too much. i think this is because with good world-building, i feel like i am looking at a kind of work of art created by the author - a rather nerdy work of art, sure - but still something that a person has put a lot of thought, energy, and passion into. i really respond to all those details that the author is in love with sharing. but maybe i just have a high threshold for these kinds of things, as i'm also the kind of person who likes to hear all the details in a person's dreams.<br /><br />Rendezvous takes world-building to a different sort of place: Clarke is <i>artifact-building</i>. the amazing alien spaceship Rama is indeed amazing; almost the entire novel is devoted to exploring this gigantic vessel. most of the narrative is in service to purely descriptive passages of Rama; everything else is either minimal characterization or political discussions from various scientists &amp; ambassador types about how to respond to Rama. all of this very focused world-building has the potential for much boredom and irritation. but i never felt that; the author's love for his creation is too clear, his details are too meticulous, his sense of wonder and his ability to concretely illustrate the almost-unknowable are too skilled, too palpable. despite my feeling that this novel essentially functions as a prologue to the 'real' action to come, i got caught up in Clarke's passion and enjoyed it all.<br /><br />for such a man of science and large-scale concepts, Clarke is a surprisingly warm writer. his characters are pleasant - and real. there are no grand villains, at least not in this initial volume of the series. and he has a sense of humor - particularly around sex (one character is described as having no interest in anything outside of work, except for sports and sex - preferably combined; a high-level scholar is described as originally making his reputation through researching "puberty rites in late-twentieth-century Beverly Hills"). for all of the high-falutin' ideas on display, there is zero pretension present in Rendezvous.<br /><br />although the novel ends before anything actually happens, there does seem to be interesting directions that the series could go. the slight mining of sexuality and gender roles could lead somewhere. and politics - particularly around how government responds to the unknown - are clearly an intriguing next step. i'm looking forward to seeing how this series pans out.<br /><br />all that said, as far as Giant Mysterious Alien Artifacts go, right now my favorite is still Greg Bear's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/840278.Eon" title="Eon by Greg Bear" rel="nofollow noopener">Eon</a> - which in many ways appears to be an homage to Rama.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6179858910794906206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_446509896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/446509896" />
    <a title="Henry Avila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5431458-henry-avila"><img alt="Henry Avila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307597403p2/5431458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/446509896?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henry Avila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henry Avila" href="/user/show/5431458-henry-avila">Henry Avila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553287899" href="/book/show/774928.Rendezvous_with_Rama">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer446509896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4032159894367464791">A large ominous object is discovered entering a remote part of the Solar System in 2131, an impressive thirty miles long and heading in the direction of Earth.You can imagine the implications, indeed... causing a little nervousness back on our world, everyone knows what happened in 2077. If you don't remember since it hasn't occurred yet a large fireball hit the Earth killing hundreds of thousand of people, devastating the great cities and untold trillions of dollars in damages. At last in Proje</span>
  <span id="freeText4032159894367464791" style="display:none">A large ominous object is discovered entering a remote part of the Solar System in 2131, an impressive thirty miles long and heading in the direction of Earth.You can imagine the implications, indeed... causing a little nervousness back on our world, everyone knows what happened in 2077. If you don't remember since it hasn't occurred yet a large fireball hit the Earth killing hundreds of thousand of people, devastating the great cities and untold trillions of dollars in damages. At last in Project Spaceguard an early warning system was established, a kind of shield can be formed which protects precious Terra from being pulverized again by a roaming asteroid.They also tract the 500,000 space boulders found in the mystifying region between the orbits of distant Mars and Jupiter however now more than fifty years later a new crises arises. Can Spaceguard save us? If it collides with the third planet , Earth will be no more than a memory good or bad. Quickly acquiring the name Rama this large rock (from a Hindu God) , the object keeps surprising us , after a space probe takes pictures it's not an asteroid but an alien spaceship of tremendous size. The long feared aliens have arrived , peaceful or otherwise that is the question? Computer analysis shows the trajectory of Rama will miss Earth and go around the back side of the Sun out into the uncharted, blackness of deep Space, never we hope to return here again. Problem solved right, if you're a sci-fi fan you know better, but humans are not very trusting beings. So the spaceship Endeavour is sent to investigate in command is Captain Norton.When the crew of the Endeavour, finally get inside Rama they are amazed the alien spacecraft, is really a new , vast, strange world to say the least.The only way down to the bottom of Rama are stairways many miles in length, in the darkness so they go, try that folks! Even in low gravity creatures seen below are half animal and half robot"Biot", as they're named by the invaders and look peaceful still where are the Ramans...A large enchanting calm Sea, who believes their eyes here is also discovered by the people from Earth. Great "cities," weird blue lights and exotic structures unexplained atmospheric storms, electrical discharges this Noah's Ark has it all except answers.The crew of the Endeavour will they ever be able to solve the mystery of Rama,the alien craft is getting hotter and hotter as it nears the scorching Sun, time is limited so the explorers must work fast. If the crew could somehow get over the high cliff blocking them and into the unknown, south pole area of Rama . Maybe all the secrets will be explained....A glorious walk into the never-ending place we call imagination...</span>
  <a data-text-id="4032159894367464791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2126959779" />
    <a title="Duane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24389390-duane"><img alt="Duane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403316391p2/24389390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2126959779?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duane" href="/user/show/24389390-duane">Duane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24389390-duane?shelf=2017-book-challenge">2017-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24389390-duane?shelf=rated-books">rated-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24389390-duane?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24389390-duane?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>,

<div id="review_2224219129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2224219129" />
    <a title="Simon Clark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53209373-simon-clark"><img alt="Simon Clark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532796330p2/53209373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2224219129?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simon Clark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simon Clark" href="/user/show/53209373-simon-clark">Simon Clark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2224219129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12600328836283719771">Strange read, but I really liked it. <br/><br/>This was my first Arthur C. Clarke - though the movie adaptation of 2001 is one of my all-time favourites that I've repeatedly rewatched - and definitely will not be my last. As sci fi nerd with scientific training from the west country, on paper Clarke (no relation) should be my perfect author. And <i>Rendezvous with Rama</i> is dead on the bullseye of my interests. It blends hard, hard sci-fi with the kind of near-futurism that I find fascinating, and succeeds in </span>
  <span id="freeText12600328836283719771" style="display:none">Strange read, but I really liked it. <br /><br />This was my first Arthur C. Clarke - though the movie adaptation of 2001 is one of my all-time favourites that I've repeatedly rewatched - and definitely will not be my last. As sci fi nerd with scientific training from the west country, on paper Clarke (no relation) should be my perfect author. And <i>Rendezvous with Rama</i> is dead on the bullseye of my interests. It blends hard, hard sci-fi with the kind of near-futurism that I find fascinating, and succeeds in creating a seriously spooky ambience in a compelling scenario: the first extraterrestrial object, clearly artificial, to enter the solar system.<br /><br />Yet despite hitting all of my buttons, and being breezily written (I read the whole book in maybe three sittings) I found it strikingly uncompelling in a few ways. Clarke - and maybe this common to his writing, or just to this book (I'll need to find out) - seems bizarrely indifferent to the niceties of characterisation. A character is frequently introduced as, for example, Claire who is a sailor. Tom who is a cyclist. Mary who is a doctor. These individuals are then used according to their one note characters in the melody of a story which has no real overarching structure. Perhaps it's because of the hyper-realism of hard sci fi, but there was no traditional story structure to speak of. Or if there was one - and there kind of is to do with the Hermians - it had no tension whatsoever. <br /><br />In short, the setting and ideas are fantastic, and this has some of my favourite world building I've ever seen in sci-fi. Undoubtedly this was incredibly influential on stories told afterwards. But the story that was told in that setting was - to me - severely lacking.<br /><br />Still, looking forward to reading more Clarke!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12600328836283719771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
